4984</section>

4985<section id="_1968">

4986<h3 id="_1968_toc">

4987Treatment of Childhood Pineoblastoma</h3>

4988<section id="_1969">

4989<h4 id="_1969_toc">

4990Treatment of children aged 3 years and younger</h4>

4991<p id="_2017" tabindex="-1">

4992Standard treatment options for children aged 3 years and younger with pineoblastoma include the following:</p>

4993<div class="pdq-content-list">

4994<ol id="_2018">

4995<li>

4996<a href="/types/brain/hp/child-cns-embryonal-treatment-pdq#_2030">

4997Biopsy (for diagnosis) and total resection, if possible</a>

4998.</li>

4999<li>

5000<a href="/types/brain/hp/child-cns-embryonal-treatment-pdq#_2031">

5001Adjuvant chemotherapy</a>

5002.</li>

5003<li>

5004<a href="/types/brain/hp/child-cns-embryonal-treatment-pdq#_2032">

5005High-dose, marrow-ablative chemotherapy with autologous bone marrow rescue or peripheral stem cell rescue</a>

5006.</li>

5007</ol>

5008</div>

5009<section id="_2030">

5010<h5 id="_2030_toc">

5011Biopsy</h5>

5012<p id="_433" tabindex="-1">

5013Biopsy and, if possible, total resection, is usually performed to diagnose pineoblastoma.</p>

5014</section>

5015<section id="_2031">

5016<h5 id="_2031_toc">

5017Adjuvant chemotherapy</h5>

5018<p id="_60" tabindex="-1">

5019Children aged 3 years and younger with pineoblastoma are usually treated initially with chemotherapy in the hope of delaying, if not obviating, the need for radiation therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_4.15">

502015</a>

5021] Overall prognosis for this group remains very poor.[<a href="#cit/section_4.7">

50227</a>

5023] In two sequential, multicenter, prospective clinical trials, all five children younger than 3 years who were treated with chemotherapy died.[<a href="#cit/section_4.16">

502416</a>

5025][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5026Level of evidence B4</a>

5027] In children responding to chemotherapy, the timing and amount of radiation therapy required after chemotherapy is unclear. The addition of craniospinal irradiation to chemotherapy-based regimens may successfully treat some children but with anticipated neurodevelopmental decline.[<a href="#cit/section_4.17">

502817</a>

5029][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5030Level of evidence B4</a>

5031]</p>

5032</section>

5033<section id="_2032">

5034<h5 id="_2032_toc">

5035High-dose, marrow-ablative chemotherapy with autologous bone marrow rescue or peripheral stem cell rescue</h5>

5036<p id="_434" tabindex="-1">

5037High-dose, marrow-ablative chemotherapy with autologous bone marrow rescue or peripheral stem cell rescue has been used with some success in young children.[<a href="#cit/section_4.18">

503818</a>

5039][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5040Level of evidence B4</a>

5041]</p>

5042</section>

5043</section>

5044<section id="_1970">

5045<h4 id="_1970_toc">

5046Treatment of children older than 3 years</h4>

5047<p id="_513" tabindex="-1">

5048Standard treatment options for children older than 3 years with newly diagnosed pineoblastoma include the following:</p>

5049<div class="pdq-content-list">

5050<ol id="_514">

5051<li>

5052<a href="/types/brain/hp/child-cns-embryonal-treatment-pdq#_1971">

5053Surgery</a>

5054.</li>

5055<li>

5056<a href="/types/brain/hp/child-cns-embryonal-treatment-pdq#_1973">

5057Adjuvant radiation therapy.</a>

5058</li>

5059<li>

5060<a href="/types/brain/hp/child-cns-embryonal-treatment-pdq#_2020">

5061Adjuvant chemotherapy</a>

5062.</li>

5063</ol>

5064</div>

5065<section id="_1971">

5066<h5 id="_1971_toc">

5067Surgery</h5>

5068<p id="_517" tabindex="-1">

5069Surgery is usually the initial treatment for patients with pineoblastoma to diagnose the tumor.[<a href="#cit/section_4.19">

507019</a>

5071] Total resections have been associated with better outcomes.</p>

5072</section>

5073<section id="_1973">

5074<h5 id="_1973_toc">

5075Adjuvant radiation therapy</h5>

5076<p id="_519" tabindex="-1">

5077The usual postsurgical treatment for patients with pineoblastoma begins with radiation therapy, although some trials have used preradiation chemotherapy. The total dose of radiation therapy to the tumor site is 54 Gy to 55.8 Gy using conventional fractionation.[<a href="#cit/section_4.13">

507813</a>

5079,<a href="#cit/section_4.14">

508014</a>

5081]</p>

5082<p id="_2019" tabindex="-1">

5083Craniospinal irradiation with doses of 23.4 Gy to 36 Gy are also recommended because of the propensity of this tumor to disseminate throughout the subarachnoid space.[<a href="#cit/section_4.7">

50847</a>

5085,<a href="#cit/section_4.13">

508613</a>

5087,<a href="#cit/section_4.14">

508814</a>

5089]</p>

5090</section>

5091<section id="_2020">

5092<h5 id="_2020_toc">

5093Adjuvant chemotherapy</h5>

5094<p id="_2021" tabindex="-1">

5095Chemotherapy is usually used in the same way as outlined for high-risk medulloblastomas in children with nondisseminated disease at the time of diagnosis. For more information, see the <a href="/types/brain/hp/child-cns-embryonal-treatment-pdq#_38">

5096Treatment of children older than 3 years with high-risk medulloblastoma</a>

5097 section.</p>

5098<p id="_2022" tabindex="-1">

5099The 5-year disease-free survival rate exceeds 50% in children with localized disease at diagnosis who undergo aggressive resection.[<a href="#cit/section_4.13">

510013</a>

5101,<a href="#cit/section_4.14">

510214</a>

5103,<a href="#cit/section_4.20">

510420</a>

5105,<a href="#cit/section_4.21">

510621</a>

5107][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5108Level of evidence A1</a>

5109] The Children's Oncology Group (COG) <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00392327">

5110COG-ACNS0332 (NCT00392327)</a>

5111 study of 36 patients with nonmedulloblastoma embryonal tumors (which included 26 pineoblastomas) reported a 5-year overall survival (OS) rate of 78.5% (95% confidence interval, 62.2%&#8211;94.8%).[<a href="#cit/section_4.21">

511221</a>

5113][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5114Level of evidence A1</a>

5115]</p>

5116<p id="_2023" tabindex="-1">

5117For patients with disseminated disease at the time of diagnosis, survival is considerably poorer.[<a href="#cit/section_4.13">

511813</a>

5119,<a href="#cit/section_4.14">

512014</a>

5121] In the <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00392327">

5122COG-ACNS0332 (NCT00392327)</a>

5123 study, there was no significant difference in event-free survival or OS according to metastatic status.</p>

5124</section>

5125</section>

5126<section id="_1974">

5127<h4 id="_1974_toc">

5128Treatment options under clinical evaluation for childhood pineoblastoma</h4>

5129<p id="_58" tabindex="-1">

5130For patients with pineoblastoma, a variety of different treatment approaches are under evaluation, including the use of higher doses of chemotherapy after radiation therapy supported by peripheral stem cell rescue and the use of chemotherapy during radiation therapy.</p>

5131<p id="_1813" tabindex="-1">

5132Early-phase therapeutic trials may be available for selected patients. These trials may be available via the <a href="https://www.childrensoncologygroup.org/" title="https://www.childrensoncologygroup.org/">

5133COG</a>

5134, the <a href="https://www.pbtc.org/" title="https://www.pbtc.org/">

5135Pediatric Brain Tumor Consortium</a>

5136, or other entities. Information about National Cancer Institute (NCI)&#8211;supported clinical trials can be found on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search">

5137NCI website</a>

5138. For information about clinical trials sponsored by other organizations, see the <a href="https://clinicaltrials.gov/" title="https://clinicaltrials.gov/">

5139ClinicalTrials.gov website</a>

5140.</p>

5141</section>

5142</section>

J Clin Oncol : JCO2017764720, 2018.&#160;<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=30332335&amp;dopt=Abstract" title="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=30332335&amp;dopt=Abstract">

5224[PUBMED Abstract]</a>

5225</li>

5226</ol>

5227</div>

5228

5229 </section>

5230

5231

5232

5233 <section id="_71">

5234

5235 <h2>

5236Treatment of Recurrent Childhood Medulloblastoma and Other CNS Embryonal Tumors</h2>

5237

5238 <div id="_section_71" class="pdq-sections">

5239<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

5240<h6>

5241In This Section</h6>

5242<ul>

5243<li>

5244<a href="#_530_toc">

5245Treatment Options<ul>

5246<li>

5247<a href="#_448_toc">

5248Surgery</a>

5249</li>

5250<li>

5251<a href="#_450_toc">

5252Radiation therapy</a>

5253</li>

5254<li>

5255<a href="#_452_toc">

5256Chemotherapy</a>

5257</li>

5258<li>

5259<a href="#_456_toc">

5260High-dose chemotherapy with stem cell rescue</a>

5261</li>

5262<li>

5263<a href="#_723_toc">

5264Molecularly targeted therapy</a>

5265</li>

5266</ul>

5267</a>

5268</li>

5269<li>

5270<a href="#_1797_toc">

5271Treatment Options Under Clinical Evaluation for Recurrent Childhood Medulloblastoma and Other CNS Embryonal Tumors<ul>

5272<li>

5273<a href="#_TrialSearch_1797_sid_6_toc">

5274Current Clinical Trials</a>

5275</li>

5276</ul>

5277</a>

5278</li>

5279</ul>

5280</nav>

5281<p id="_72" tabindex="-1">

5282Recurrence of all forms of central nervous system (CNS) embryonal tumors is not uncommon and usually occurs within 36 months of treatment. However, recurrent tumors may also develop many years after initial treatment.[<a href="#cit/section_5.1">

52831</a>

5284-<a href="#cit/section_5.3">

52853</a>

5286] In such late relapses, especially those occurring 5 or more years after diagnosis, differentiation from secondary tumors such as high-grade gliomas can be difficult, and histological confirmation is recommended and usually required. In a 2021 report, a paired molecular cohort was assembled, consisting of 127 patients with tissue specimens available from both their primary medulloblastoma and subsequent tumors associated with relapse. Comparative molecular analyses were performed using the patient-matched tumor specimens. DNA methylation-based classification identified nine relapse cases (7%) as histologies other than medulloblastoma.[<a href="#cit/section_5.4">

52874</a>

5288] Disease may recur at the primary site or may be disseminated at the time of relapse. Sites of noncontiguous relapse may include the spinal leptomeninges, intracranial sites, and cerebrospinal fluid, in isolation or in any combination, and may be associated with primary tumor relapse.[<a href="#cit/section_5.1">

52891</a>

5290,<a href="#cit/section_5.2">

52912</a>

5292,<a href="#cit/section_5.5">

52935</a>

5294] Extraneural disease relapse may occur but is rare and is seen primarily in patients who were treated with radiation therapy alone.[<a href="#cit/section_5.6">

52956</a>

5296][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5297Level of evidence C1</a>

5298]</p>

5299<p id="_654" tabindex="-1">

5300Studies have found that even in patients with nondisseminated disease at diagnosis, and independent of the dose of radiation therapy or the type of chemotherapy, approximately one-third of patients will relapse at the primary tumor site alone, one-third will relapse at the primary tumor site plus distant sites, and one-third will relapse at distant sites without relapse at the primary site.[<a href="#cit/section_5.1">

53011</a>

5302,<a href="#cit/section_5.2">

53032</a>

5304,<a href="#cit/section_5.5">

53055</a>

5306] </p>

5307<section id="_530">

5308<h3 id="_530_toc">

5309Treatment Options</h3>

5310<p id="_531" tabindex="-1">

5311There are no standard treatment options for recurrent childhood CNS embryonal tumors. For more information, see the <a href="/types/brain/hp/child-cns-atrt-treatment-pdq#_55">

5312Treatment for Recurrent Childhood CNS Atypical Teratoid/Rhabdoid Tumor</a>

5313 section in Childhood Central Nervous System Atypical Teratoid/Rhabdoid Tumor Treatment.</p>

5314<p id="_655" tabindex="-1">

5315For most children, treatment is palliative, and disease control is transient in patients previously treated with radiation therapy and chemotherapy, with more than 80% of patients progressing within 2 years.[<a href="#cit/section_5.3">

53163</a>

5317]; [<a href="#cit/section_5.7">

53187</a>

5319][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5320Level of evidence C1</a>

5321] For young children, predominantly those younger than 3 years at diagnosis who were never treated with radiation therapy, longer-term control with reoperation, radiation therapy, and chemotherapy is possible.[<a href="#cit/section_5.5">

53225</a>

5323,<a href="#cit/section_5.8">

53248</a>

5325-<a href="#cit/section_5.11">

532611</a>

5327]</p>

5328<p id="_656" tabindex="-1">

5329Treatment approaches may include the following:</p>

5330<div class="pdq-content-list">

5331<ol id="_532">

5332<li>

5333<a href="/types/brain/hp/child-cns-embryonal-treatment-pdq#_448">

5334Surgery</a>

5335.</li>

5336<li>

5337<a href="/types/brain/hp/child-cns-embryonal-treatment-pdq#_450">

5338Radiation therapy</a>

5339.</li>

5340<li>

5341<a href="/types/brain/hp/child-cns-embryonal-treatment-pdq#_452">

5342Chemotherapy</a>

5343.</li>

5344<li>

5345<a href="/types/brain/hp/child-cns-embryonal-treatment-pdq#_456">

5346High-dose chemotherapy with stem cell rescue</a>

5347.</li>

5348<li>

5349<a href="/types/brain/hp/child-cns-embryonal-treatment-pdq#_723">

5350Molecularly targeted therapy</a>

5351.</li>

5352</ol>

5353</div>

5354<section id="_448">

5355<h4 id="_448_toc">

5356Surgery</h4>

5357<p id="_449" tabindex="-1">

5358At the time of relapse, a complete evaluation for extent of recurrence is indicated for all embryonal tumors. Biopsy or surgical resection may be necessary for confirmation of relapse because other entities, such as secondary tumors and treatment-related brain necrosis, may be clinically indistinguishable from tumor recurrence. The need for surgical intervention must be individualized on the basis of the initial tumor type, the length of time between initial treatment and the reappearance of the lesion, and clinical symptoms. </p>

5359</section>

5360<section id="_450">

5361<h4 id="_450_toc">

5362Radiation therapy</h4>

5363<p id="_451" tabindex="-1">

5364Patients with recurrent embryonal tumors who have already received radiation therapy and chemotherapy may be candidates for further radiation therapy depending on the site and dose of previous radiation. Treatment may include reirradiation at the primary tumor site, focal areas of radiation therapy to sites of disseminated disease, and craniospinal radiation therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_5.12">

536512</a>

5366,<a href="#cit/section_5.13">

536713</a>

5368] However, long-term survival has been observed in a subset of patients who received chemotherapy alone at the time of diagnosis and had local relapse. This finding was primarily noted in young children with sonic hedgehog (SHH)&#8211;activated disease.[<a href="#cit/section_5.14">

536914</a>

5370] In most cases, such therapy is palliative. Stereotactic radiation therapy and/or salvage chemotherapy can also be used.[<a href="#cit/section_5.15">

537115</a>

5372] For more information, see the <a href="/types/brain/hp/child-cns-embryonal-treatment-pdq#_452">

5373Chemotherapy</a>

5374 section.</p>

5375</section>

5376<section id="_452">

5377<h4 id="_452_toc">

5378Chemotherapy</h4>

5379<p id="_2024" tabindex="-1">

5380Recurrent CNS embryonal tumors can respond to chemotherapeutic agents used singularly or in combination, including cyclophosphamide, cisplatin, carboplatin, lomustine, etoposide, topotecan, temozolomide, the combination of irinotecan and temozolomide with or without bevacizumab, and antiangiogenic metronomic therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_5.8">

53818</a>

5382,<a href="#cit/section_5.16">

538316</a>

5384-<a href="#cit/section_5.26">

538526</a>

5386]; [<a href="#cit/section_5.27">

538727</a>

5388,<a href="#cit/section_5.28">

538928</a>

5390][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5391Level of evidence B4</a>

5392] Approximately 30% to 50% of these patients will have objective responses to conventional chemotherapy, but long-term disease control is rare. </p>

5393<p id="_2025" tabindex="-1">

5394For select patients with recurrent medulloblastoma&#8212;primarily infants and young children who were treated at the time of diagnosis with chemotherapy alone and who developed local recurrence&#8212;long-term disease control may be obtained after further treatment with chemotherapy plus local radiation therapy. This potential may be greatest in patients who are able to undergo complete resection of the recurrent disease.[<a href="#cit/section_5.29">

539529</a>

5396][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5397Level of evidence B4</a>

5398]; [<a href="#cit/section_5.30">

539930</a>

5400][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5401Level of evidence C1</a>

5402] </p>

5403<p id="_2026" tabindex="-1">

5404In a St. Jude Children&#8217;s Research Hospital study (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00602667">

5405SJYC07 [NCT00602667])</a>

5406, 29 patients with progressive disease received craniospinal irradiation (median dose, 36 Gy; interquartile range, 36&#8211;36). Of these 29 patients, 18 (62%) were alive at the time of publication, compared with 6 of 25 patients (24%) who did not receive craniospinal irradiation.[<a href="#cit/section_5.11">

540711</a>

5408][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5409Level of evidence B4</a>

5410]</p>

5411</section>

5412<section id="_456">

5413<h4 id="_456_toc">

5414High-dose chemotherapy with stem cell rescue</h4>

5415<p id="_457" tabindex="-1">

5416For patients who have previously received radiation therapy, higher-dose chemotherapeutic regimens, supported with autologous bone marrow rescue or peripheral stem cell support, have been used with variable results.[<a href="#cit/section_5.9">

54179</a>

5418,<a href="#cit/section_5.10">

541910</a>

5420,<a href="#cit/section_5.31">

542131</a>

5422-<a href="#cit/section_5.34">

542334</a>

5424][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5425Level of evidence B4</a>

5426]; [<a href="#cit/section_5.35">

542735</a>

5428-<a href="#cit/section_5.37">

542937</a>

5430][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5431Level of evidence C1</a>

5432]</p>

5433<div class="pdq-content-list">

5434<ol id="_458">

5435<li>

5436With such regimens, objective response is frequent, occurring in 50% to 75% of patients. However, long-term disease control is obtained in fewer than 30% of patients and is seen primarily in patients in first relapse and in those with only localized disease at the time of relapse.[<a href="#cit/section_5.10">

543710</a>

5438]; [<a href="#cit/section_5.34">

543934</a>

5440][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5441Level of evidence B4</a>

5442]; [<a href="#cit/section_5.35">

544335</a>

5444][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5445Level of evidence C1</a>

5446]</li>

5447<li>

5448Additionally, results from national trials for relapsed medulloblastoma that specified intent to transplant as part of their treatment plan showed that only approximately 5% of patients initiating retrieval therapy achieved long-term disease-free survival with this strategy.[<a href="#cit/section_5.34">

544934</a>

5450,<a href="#cit/section_5.38">

545138</a>

5452] Thus, studies that report from the time of transplant overestimate the benefit of transplant-based approaches for the total population of relapsing patients.</li>

5453<li>

5454Long-term disease control for patients with disseminated disease is infrequent.[<a href="#cit/section_5.39">

545539</a>

5456][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5457Level of evidence C1</a>

5458]</li>

5459</ol>

5460</div>

5461</section>

5462<section id="_723">

5463<h4 id="_723_toc">

5464Molecularly targeted therapy</h4>

5465<p id="_724" tabindex="-1">

5466

5467With increased knowledge of the molecular and genetic changes associated with different subtypes of medulloblastoma, molecularly targeted therapy, also called precision therapy, is being actively explored in children with recurrent disease. </p>

5468<p id="_2027" tabindex="-1">

5469In patients with recurrent SHH-activated medulloblastomas, the SHH <em class="gene-name">

5470PTCH1</em>

5471 inhibitor vismodegib demonstrated radiographic responses in 3 of 12 pediatric-aged patients, with two responses being sustained for less than 2 months and one response for more than 6 months. Only patients with upstream mutations of the SHH pathway, at the level of <em class="gene-name">

5472PTCH1</em>

5473 or <em class="gene-name">

5474SMO</em>

5475, responded.[<a href="#cit/section_5.40">

547640</a>

5477] However, because of the development of irreversible growth plate fusions, the use of vismodegib is limited to skeletally mature children.[<a href="#cit/section_5.41">

547841</a>

5479]</p>

5480</section>

5481</section>

5482<section id="_1797">

5483<h3 id="_1797_toc">

5484Treatment Options Under Clinical Evaluation for Recurrent Childhood Medulloblastoma and Other CNS Embryonal Tumors</h3>

5485<p id="_1798" tabindex="-1">

5486Early-phase therapeutic trials may be available for selected patients. These trials may be available via the <a href="https://www.childrensoncologygroup.org/" title="https://www.childrensoncologygroup.org/">

5487Children's Oncology Group (COG)</a>

5488, the <a href="https://www.pbtc.org/" title="https://www.pbtc.org/">

5489Pediatric Brain Tumor Consortium</a>

5490, or other entities. Information about National Cancer Institute (NCI)&#8211;supported clinical trials can be found on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search">

5491NCI website</a>

5492. For information about clinical trials sponsored by other organizations, see the <a href="https://clinicaltrials.gov/" title="https://clinicaltrials.gov/">

5493ClinicalTrials.gov website</a>

5494.</p>

5495<p id="_1814" tabindex="-1">

5496The following is an example of a national and/or institutional clinical trial that is currently being conducted:</p>

5497<div class="pdq-content-list">

5498<ul id="_1799">

5499<li>

5500<strong>

5501<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT03155620">

5502APEC1621 (NCT03155620)</a>

5503</strong>

5504 (Pediatric MATCH: Targeted Therapy Directed by Genetic Testing in Treating Pediatric Patients with Relapsed or Refractory Advanced Solid Tumors, Non-Hodgkin Lymphomas, or Histiocytic Disorders)<strong>

5505:</strong>

5506 NCI-COG Pediatric Molecular Analysis for Therapeutic Choice (MATCH), referred to as Pediatric MATCH, will match targeted agents with specific molecular changes identified in a patient's tumor (refractory or recurrent). Children and adolescents aged 1 to 21 years are eligible for the trial.<p id="_1807" tabindex="-1">

5507Patients with tumors that have molecular variants addressed by treatment arms included in the trial will be offered treatment on Pediatric MATCH. Additional information can be obtained on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/nci-supported/pediatric-match" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/nci-supported/pediatric-match">

5508NCI website</a>

5509 and <a href="https://clinicaltrials.gov/ct2/show/NCT03155620" title="https://clinicaltrials.gov/ct2/show/NCT03155620">

5510ClinicalTrials.gov website</a>

5511.</p>

5512

5513</li>

5514</ul>

5515</div>

5516<section id="_TrialSearch_1797_sid_6">

5517<h4 id="_TrialSearch_1797_sid_6_toc">

5518Current Clinical Trials</h4>

5519<p id="_TrialSearch_1797_22" tabindex="-1">

5520Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

5521advanced clinical trial search</a>

5522 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

5523General information</a>

5524 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

5756 <section id="_AboutThis_1">

5757

5758 <h2>

5759About This PDQ Summary</h2>

5760

5761 <div id="_section_AboutThis_1" class="pdq-sections">

5762<section id="_AboutThis_2">

5763<h3 id="_AboutThis_2_toc">

5764Purpose of This Summary</h3>

5765<p id="_AboutThis_3" tabindex="-1">

5766This PDQ cancer information summary for health professionals provides comprehensive, peer-reviewed, evidence-based information about the treatment of childhood medulloblastoma and other central nervous system embryonal tumors. It is intended as a resource to inform and assist clinicians in the care of their patients. It does not provide formal guidelines or recommendations for making health care decisions.</p>

5767</section>

5768<section id="_AboutThis_4">

5769<h3 id="_AboutThis_4_toc">

5770Reviewers and Updates</h3>

5771<p id="_AboutThis_5" tabindex="-1">

5772This summary is reviewed regularly and updated as necessary by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/pediatric-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/pediatric-treatment">

5773PDQ Pediatric Treatment Editorial Board</a>

5774, which is editorially independent of the National Cancer Institute (NCI). The summary reflects an independent review of the literature and does not represent a policy statement of NCI or the National Institutes of Health (NIH).</p>

5775<p id="_AboutThis_22" tabindex="-1">

5776 Board members review recently published articles each month to determine whether an article should:</p>

5777<div class="pdq-content-list">

5778<ul id="_AboutThis_6">

5779<li>

5780be discussed at a meeting,</li>

5781<li>

5782be cited with text, or</li>

5783<li>

5784replace or update an existing article that is already cited.</li>

5785</ul>

5786</div>

5787<p id="_AboutThis_7" tabindex="-1">

5788Changes to the summaries are made through a consensus process in which Board members evaluate the strength of the evidence in the published articles and determine how the article should be included in the summary.</p>

5789<p id="" tabindex="-1">

5790The lead reviewers for Childhood Medulloblastoma and Other Central Nervous System Embryonal Tumors Treatment are:</p>

5791<div class="pdq-content-list">

5792<ul id="">

5793<li>

5794Kenneth J. Cohen, MD, MBA (Sidney Kimmel Comprehensive Cancer Center at Johns Hopkins Hospital)</li>

5795<li>

5796Louis S. Constine, MD (James P. Wilmot Cancer Center at University of Rochester Medical Center)</li>

5797<li>

5798Roger J. Packer, MD (Children's National Hospital)</li>

5799<li>

5802Malcolm A. Smith, MD, PhD (National Cancer Institute)</li>

5803</ul>

5804</div>

5805<p id="_AboutThis_9" tabindex="-1">

5806Any comments or questions about the summary content should be submitted to Cancer.gov through the NCI website's <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us" title="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us">

5807Email Us</a>

5808. Do not contact the individual Board Members with questions or comments about the summaries. Board members will not respond to individual inquiries.</p>

5809</section>

5810<section id="_AboutThis_10">

5811<h3 id="_AboutThis_10_toc">

5812Levels of Evidence</h3>

5813<p id="_AboutThis_11" tabindex="-1">

5814Some of the reference citations in this summary are accompanied by a level-of-evidence designation. These designations are intended to help readers assess the strength of the evidence supporting the use of specific interventions or approaches. The PDQ Pediatric Treatment Editorial Board uses a <a href="/publications/pdq/levels-evidence/treatment">

5815formal evidence ranking system</a>

5816 in developing its level-of-evidence designations.</p>

5817</section>

5818<section id="_AboutThis_12">

5819<h3 id="_AboutThis_12_toc">

5820Permission to Use This Summary</h3>

5821<p id="_AboutThis_13" tabindex="-1">

5822PDQ is a registered trademark. Although the content of PDQ documents can be used freely as text, it cannot be identified as an NCI PDQ cancer information summary unless it is presented in its entirety and is regularly updated. However, an author would be permitted to write a sentence such as &#8220;NCI&#8217;s PDQ cancer information summary about breast cancer prevention states the risks succinctly: [include excerpt from the summary].&#8221;</p>

5823<p id="_AboutThis_14" tabindex="-1">

5824The preferred citation for this PDQ summary is:</p>

5825<p id="_AboutThis_15" tabindex="-1">

5826PDQ&#174; Pediatric Treatment Editorial Board. PDQ Childhood Medulloblastoma and Other Central Nervous System Embryonal Tumors Treatment. Bethesda, MD: National Cancer Institute. Updated &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. Available at: <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/types/brain/hp/child-cns-embryonal-treatment-pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/types/brain/hp/child-cns-embryonal-treatment-pdq">

5827https://www.cancer.gov/types/brain/hp/child-cns-embryonal-treatment-pdq</a>

5828. Accessed &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. [PMID: 26389418]</p>

5830Images in this summary are used with permission of the author(s), artist, and/or publisher for use within the PDQ summaries only. Permission to use images outside the context of PDQ information must be obtained from the owner(s) and cannot be granted by the National Cancer Institute. Information about using the illustrations in this summary, along with many other cancer-related images, is available in <a href="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/" title="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/">

5836<section id="_AboutThis_17">

5837<h3 id="_AboutThis_17_toc">

5838Disclaimer</h3>

5839<p id="_AboutThis_18" tabindex="-1">

5840Based on the strength of the available evidence, treatment options may be described as either &#8220;standard&#8221; or &#8220;under clinical evaluation.&#8221; These classifications should not be used as a basis for insurance reimbursement determinations. More information on insurance coverage is available on Cancer.gov on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/managing-care" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/managing-care">

5841Managing Cancer Care</a>

5842 page.</p>
